  56. I've had these brushes for about two months.<br /><br />First- Maintenance. Always wash and moisturize new brushes before they touch your face or your makeup. If you don't know how to wash and oil brushes, go to youtube and search for how to care of makeup brushes. When the brushes are mad, they are exposed to all types of chemicals. You have to get that off of the natural hair brushes and get the hair oiled to keep their moisture. They also pick up chemicals when they are packaged, especially in a newly dyed leather case; it will make them stink. So, clean them well, let them dry completely, and they are good to go.<br /><br />Second- Smell. Yes, the case does have a smell. Its from the die. Yes, the case is leather. That horrid stench is from the dyes they have to use to dye the leather. It's perfectly normal, and how you get rid of it? DON'T WASH IT. Take all your brushes out, but them into a safe box and then stick your case out in the dry open air. Give it a few days to just &#34;air out&#34;. Mine was particularly bad, but after a week in the open air, some saddle soap, and a day in the desert sun and a night in the desert cold, the case smells fine now. After a couple months in the house, the smell is completely gone and the leather is supple and strong.<br /><br />Third- Packaging. It was well packaged and everything arrived in perfect condition.<br /><br />Fourth- Use. These are excellent brushes, they pick up product well, they hold it fair enough that you wont be leaving a dusting of powder when you use them but they are very easy to clean. Their manufacture is strong and sturdy without being too heavy. They are well balanced so you have good control with them regardless of what you are doing.<br /><br />Recommendation? These brushes are great for new and experienced users, but I recommend them more for new beginners. They are cheap compared to most good brushes, so if you're just starting out in your make-up exploration these brushes are perfect to get you started and they will last you as your master the glories of makeup creativity. If you maintain them, keep them clean, and keep them safe, you should have these brushes for a very long time.

  142. This set offers a really nice selection of brushes. It can be a little difficult to see what kind of brushes you are getting based on the picture, so here is what you can expect: 3 face brushes that can be used for powder, blush or bronzer. They're all slightly different sizes, but they're pretty similar. You also get a really nice fluffy fan brush. It's more like a flattened powder brush since it's at least 3 times thicker than a normal fan brush. You also get a very small detail brush that works well for lining lips or for cream/liquid eyeliner. There is also 1 sponge tip brush, which is essentially just the same sponge tip applicators that come with most eyeshadows but on a brush handle. You also get a spool brush for eye brows and a dual ended eyelash brush/comb. The remainder of the brushes are either \\"c\\" eyeshadow brushes or flat top brushes. They're all in those 2 shapes, they just come in a variety of sizes.<br /><br />The brushes are all synthetic hair, which is nice for lip products, concealer and for using eyeshadows wet, but you might find that you have some difficulty applying eyeshadows dry. It's not impossible, but the brushes tend to create a lot of fall out with dry shadows. I personally got this set to use with pigments and loose mineral shadows (which I apply wet using a makeup setting mist)and they work perfectly.<br /><br />Over all, I'm impressed. It's a nice set for the money and even though there are a ton of similar brushes it's nice to have some clean backups in my collection. In my opinion it's missing some essentials, like a foundation brush and a blending brush - but otherwise you can create a full makeup look using only these brushes.

As with any new brush, I deodorized them & then thouroughly washed them. I can see why someone would think that they had been used because of the excess dye in the natural hairs, that person obviously does not wash their new brushes before using them for the first time. After deep cleaning them & conditioning them, they stopped shedding and they smell fresh & clean. Please do a deep cleaning on these brushes before using them if you already do not clean your new brushes before first use. Deodorizing, deep cleaning & conditioning them will get all of the loose hairs & excess dye out of the brushes. The excess dye will make your coulours look dirty & muddled if you do not deep clean them. Also after deodorizing & deep cleaning the brushes, I conditioned them and they are all soft and silky just like my Shiseido, Lancome & MAC brushes, except for the synthetic ones which I did not bother conditioning with brush cleaner. I treated each & every brush with the same care as a much more expensive, pro brush & sincerely, I can't tell them apart. Buy these, take good care of them & you will be thoroughly impressed. If you do not know how to deodorize & clean new brushes check out youtube, there ar so many videos by professionals on how to take care of your brushes. Just be warned that deordorizing and cleaning all of these brushes at once takes a lot of time, but it's worth it & hopefully you will love them as much as me.by professionals on how to take care of your brushes. Just be warned that deordorizing and cleaning all of these brushes at once takes a lot of time, but it's worth it & hopefully you will love them as much as me.

One reason I would often resort to my fingers is that I didn't ever want to make a big investment in brushes as I feared I might not \\"get the hang of them\\" or find out that I wouldn't want to take the extra time/steps they demand over using the trusty fingers...so any brushes I had purchased were of the \\"discount\\" variety. Well, those brushes, barring a few, were always flimsy, too soft and \\"floppy\\" or weirdly edged so that whatever I was trying to do with the brush seemed less successful than my fingers...so, I always resorted back to the hands. When I saw this kit on Amazon, I realized it had a million brushes for a very reasonable price, so MAYBE I could find one or 2 that would work and I could, alas...be more grown-up in my technique. When the brushes got here, it was immediately evident by the feel that they were plenty dense, not floppy/flimsy etc. like most less expensive brushes. When I loaded them with product, they deposited colors evenly and with ease. Dare I say, with the exception of the \\"extra step\\", they rival my finger's capabilities.<br /><br />Multiple Sizes/Shapes; For brush gurus and newbies alike, there are plenty of sizes, shapes and \\"edges\\" to do whatever you need to do. If you have a favorite brush shape, there are at least 3 of each shape in various sizes to meet your application needs.<br /><br />Handy Case; The case is soft, supple and rolls up neatly. This is perfect for travel, tho I, myself, am far too lazy to insert each brush back in it's little designated spot each and every time I use them. An added bonus, for those less lazy than me, is that each brush comes with a durable plastic protective sleeve. I would imagine this would keep product from rubbing off on other items, and most importantly...will keep the brush shape in tact. Very nice packaging.<br /><br />CONS<br /><br />No Instructions/labeling; Okay, so most people probably don't need guidance the way I do, but it would be nice if the brushes were labeled, or even if there was a product insert that listed the most common uses for the types/shapes/sizes of brushes. As a noob, I wasn't sure which I should use for concealer, or which I should use for eyeshadow. Oh, and what was the difference between the \\"blush brushes\\" that all appeared fairly similiar? What do people use that giant fan brush for? Why are there 32384238 flat square edged brushes? What do the cool kids do with those? In other words, I was confused and found myself searching the internet for \\"guidance\\" as to what brushes are best for what. This probably is a non-issue for most, but for me, it would have been nice to have some direction as soon as I opened the package.<br /><br />A Few Stray Hairs; As a cosmetic brush noob, I can only assume that the best quality brushes don't have shedding or random \\"strays\\". I have dabled in some painting in my life, and know that longer odd hairs at a different length than the brush's \\"chisel\\", and some shedding, is to be expected from the \\"budget brands\\". While these are by no means AWFUL, buyers just need to be sure to pull on the bristles to get loose hairs out before first application. Once I did this, I didn't have any problem with additional hairs coming out. It seems that just the manufacturing process might have left the strays. I also have found a few long hair \\"randoms\\" that might need to be trimmed for the more discerning consumer. For me, those are a non issue as I'm not exactly a professional. This \\"con\\" is not major, but thought it worth mentioning.<br /><br />All Long Handled; This should be abundantly obvious from the photos, so this is not a TRUE \\"con\\", in the sense that it wasn't what you expected, but all brushes are long handled. There are a few applications where I might prefer a shorter brush. Patting on eyelid color, for example...for me would be easier to \\"control\\" with a shorter brush. I have hooded lids so trying to get the lightest color in a specific area with a giant long handle takes some getting used to. Again, this should not be a true detractor from purchasing this product as it might be a personal preference and definitely should be noted that this user has a lot of errors. LoL<br /><br />\\"Missing\\" Pencil Brush; One brush I have used in my mostly-brushless-application is a \\"pencil brush\\" (I think that is what it is called). It is a tapered \\"point\\" of a brush...not an eyeliner brush with long bristles, more dense, shorter bristles and slightly tapered/rounded. This kit did not have one of those specifically. Since I used this kind of brush to smudge eyeliner harsh lines etc., I was able to find some alternatives in the kit. I used the angled brushes (good for eyebrow filling) and or some of the smaller flat/oval/chiseled brushes to do the same thing my beloved \\"pencil brush\\" did.<br /><br />All in all, this kit is worth entertaining, especially for someone just wanting to try some new brushes and/or application techniques. The quality is quite good, which was a GREAT surprise at this price range. There is no doubt in my mind that EVERYONE will find at least a couple of brushes they love.thought it worth mentioning. NEVER place brushes upright to dry, the moisture will seep down into the brush and it will rot and smell over time. Now my brushes are very soft and workable. This is a excellent set for beginers or travel...imo worth more than $16.99...Also, if your not doing alot of detail work, the 13 piece set will work fine instead of this 24 piece set. I used elastic bands to attach the handles of the brushes to hangers, and hung them to dry, so the water wouldn't sit inside the ferrule (the metal part where the hair is glued in), because that loosens the glue.<br /><br />I was surprised at the quality of the brush handles. It's really an amazing set for the price. They wouldn't compare to expensive brushes (some of the brushes had odd cuts) but for the price, the quality is outstanding.<br /><br />I didn't feel like any of the brushes were good for applying liquid foundation. I'm hoping that when I get the other Shany kit with the angled and flat topped brushes, that it will have a better option for foundation.<br /><br />All in all, a great cheap starter set, and probably the perfect choice if you're giving them to a teenager to experiment with.   693. So I've had my SHANY makeup brushes for two weeks and thought that I gave enough time to give a fair review. I'll start by saying that I am not a professional but I am a makeup enthusiast and I think for that for what I need them for, they are good. The brushes are soft and there is a wide variety of sizes. Most of the brushes are geared towards the eyes. A lot of the brushes for eyes are a little too big to use on the eyes and end up being a little awkard but there is a good selection and most likely for everyday makeup uses you'll find a brush that suits your needs. The one complaint I have about the brush selection is that there is no kabuki.. I ended up using one of the larger blush brushes for foundation application and it actually works out quite well<br /><br />Now, I'd like to reply to some common complaints and comments I saw among other reviewers:<br /><br />As far and the case goes. It is NOT real leather. The case is made of some type of vinyl and does indeed smell pretty bad. What I did was remove all the brushes and just stood the case up in the window over night to air out. The smell went away...problem solved.<br /><br />On that note, I read a lot of people say the brushes smell bad. I did not think so at all. They may have slightly taken on the smell of the case but once they were washed it was fine.<br /><br />Speaking of washing the brushes, I also read a lot of reviewers complain about bristles falling out. Now, it is beauty 101 that when you wash your brushes you are NOT supposed to get the base wet. This will case problems with even the best of brushes as it causes weakening. To get around this I simply grip the base of the brush when I'm running them under water, using my whole hand for large brushes and the tips of my fingers for smaller brushes (for the super small ones, I don't bother). Lather with a gentle face wash and rinse. Then lay them out on a paper towel and let them dry overnight. I have not had and trouble with fallout. A couple strays here and there, but nothing major.<br /><br />For a starter kit, I think this set is great. I do plan on slowly purchasing some better quality versions of the brushes I use the most. But this is a great supplement to any makeup lover's collection. And for the price you can't beat it.

For your face I recommend the sephora pro angled blush brush #49, the sephora precision powder #59, the sephora pro flawless light powder brush #50, and of course the Mac 187 stippling brush. These have worked lovely for me. I also highly recommend the beauty blender sponges that you slightly dampen to blend foundation for beautiful streak free build able coverage. Hope this helps:)
